[4/27/23, 4:45:16 PM] Emin Turkey: As the academic year comes to a close and we prepare to part ways, I wanted to take a moment to reflect on our incredible journey together at Koç University. Our shared experiences, the strength of our community, and the challenges we overcame have shaped us into the individuals we are today.

Throughout our time at this esteemed institution, we have witnessed firsthand the resilience and unity of our diverse student body, particularly among the Azerbaijani and Turkish students. The beautiful bond between our nations, epitomized by the words of the great leader Heydar Aliyev: “One nation, two states”, has been a driving force behind our collective success.

As an Azerbaijani student, I have had the privilege of contributing to this unbreakable bond, ensuring that our camaraderie transcends borders and permeates every aspect of our lives. From study sessions to cultural exchanges, I have been honored to be an ambassador of this unity, both within our community and beyond.

During the challenging period of the liberation of globally recognized Azerbaijani lands in Karabakh from illegal Armenian occupation, our brotherly Turkish students demonstrated unwavering support and solidarity. This meaningful gesture not only bolstered our spirits but also reinforced the special bond between our two nations, reflecting the essence of unity between the young people at Koc University working towards a resilient future.

In the face of the unprecedented global pandemic, our community rose to the challenge with admirable courage and perseverance. We leaned on each other for support, adapting to new learning methods and cultivating a strong sense of togetherness, even as we navigated through the uncertainty. It is a testament to our collective strength that we stand here today, ready to embark on the next chapter of our lives. I take pride in calling myself a Koc alumni, and know for a fact that so do many others.

Looking back on the challenges we faced, the memories we created, and the friendships we forged, I am filled with immense pride and gratitude. Our time at Koç University has not only honed our academic and professional skills but also instilled in us the values of unity, resilience, and empathy.

As we graduate and move forward, let us carry these invaluable lessons with us, never forgetting the power of community and common cause. May we continue to uphold the spirit of academic unity in our future endeavors, and may the friendships and connections we formed here at Koç University last a lifetime.

Wishing all alumni the best in their future pursuits.

Emin Hidayat-zada.

[5/1/23, 12:47:06 AM] Emin Turkey: As the academic year comes to a close and we prepare to part ways, I wanted to take a moment to reflect on my incredible journey at Koç University. Our pivotal shared experiences, the strength of our community, and the challenges we overcame have shaped us into the individuals we are today.

Throughout my time at this esteemed institution, I have witnessed firsthand the resilience and unity of our diverse student body, particularly among the Azerbaijani and Turkish students. The beautiful bond between our nations, epitomized by the words of the great leader Heydar Aliyev: “One nation, two states”, has been a driving force behind our collective success.

As an Azerbaijani student, I have had the privilege of contributing to this unbreakable bond, ensuring that our camaraderie transcends borders and permeates every aspect of our lives. From study sessions to cultural exchanges, I have been honored to be an ambassador of this unity, both within our community and beyond.

During the challenging period of the liberation of Karabakh - the globally recognized territory of the Republic of Azerbaijan from the illegitimate and illegal Armenian occupation, our brotherly Turkish students demonstrated unwavering support and solidarity. As accentuated by our leader and commander in chief Ilham Aliyev “the great son of the Turkic world and outstanding leader, Mustafa Kemal Ataturk” has stated :“Azerbaijan’s grief and happiness are our own” . I am honored to say that this historic phrase was reinforced by actions of students at Koç University. This meaningful gesture not only bolstered our spirits but also reinforced the special bond between our two nations, reflecting the essence of unity between the young people at Koç University constantly working towards a resilient future.

In the face of the unprecedented global pandemic, our community rose to the challenge with admirable courage and perseverance. We leaned on each other for support, adapting to new learning methods and cultivating a strong sense of togetherness, even as we navigated through the uncertainty. It is a testament to our collective strength that we stand here today, ready to embark on the next chapter of our lives. I take pride in calling myself a Koc alumni, and know for a fact that so do many others.

Looking back on the challenges we faced, the memories we created, and the friendships we forged, I am filled with immense pride and gratitude. Our time at Koç University has not only honed our academic and professional skills but also instilled in us the values of unity, resilience, and empathy.

As we graduate and move forward, let us carry these invaluable lessons with us, never forgetting the power of community and common cause. May we continue to uphold the spirit of academic unity in our future endeavors, and may the friendships and connections we formed here at Koç University last a lifetime. 

Wishing all alumni the best in their prospective future pursuits.

Emin Hidayat-zada.

[11/27/23, 9:53:04 PM] FGK: To find the Nash equilibrium of the War of Attrition game with the given payoff functions, we consider the strategies that the players might adopt and then identify the best responses to the strategies of the other player. A Nash equilibrium occurs when each player's strategy is the best response to the other player's strategy.

The payoff functions are defined as follows:

For player 1:
\[ u_1(x_1, x_2) = \begin{cases} -x_1, & \text{if } x_1 < x_2 \\ v_1 - x_2, & \text{if } x_1 \geq x_2 \end{cases} \]

For player 2:
\[ u_2(x_1, x_2) = \begin{cases} -x_2, & \text{if } x_2 \leq x_1 \\ v_2 - x_1, & \text{if } x_2 > x_1 \end{cases} \]

A Nash equilibrium in this game will satisfy the condition that neither player can increase their payoff by unilaterally changing their own stopping time, given the stopping time of the other player.

Let's consider the best responses for each player.

For player 1, given a strategy \( x_2 \) of player 2:
- If \( x_1 < x_2 \), player 1's best response is to increase \( x_1 \) to be equal to \( x_2 \), as this would increase their payoff from negative to \( v_1 - x_2 \).
- If \( x_1 \geq x_2 \), player 1's best response is to maintain \( x_1 \) just above \( x_2 \) to ensure they get \( v_1 - x_2 \).

For player 2, given a strategy \( x_1 \) of player 1:
- If \( x_2 < x_1 \), player 2's best response is to increase \( x_2 \) to be equal to \( x_1 \), however, since player 1 wins if they give up at the same time, player 2 would prefer giving up just before \( x_1 \) to minimize their loss.
- If \( x_2 > x_1 \), player 2's best response is to reduce \( x_2 \) to be just below \( x_1 \) to win the prize with a minimal loss.

Considering the payoff structure, we can see that if both players play optimally, the game will not have a pure strategy Nash equilibrium in finite time because both players would want to give up at exactly the same moment, which is not possible here.

However, there is a mixed strategy Nash equilibrium where each player randomizes over an infinite set of possible give-up times, with a probability distribution that makes the opponent indifferent between different give-up times.

Mathematically, these mixed strategies involve solving for probability distributions such that the expected payoff for giving up at any time is the same, taking into account the probability that the other player has already given up and the costs incurred over time.

The detailed mathematical solution would involve integrating the payoff functions over the probability distributions to find the conditions that equalize the payoffs, but this requires more advanced calculus and cannot be easily shown in this format. If you have access to a mathematical or game theory textbook, they often provide step-by-step solutions to these types of problems, or if you're taking a course, your instructor should be able to guide you through the process.
